</TABLE> <P STYLE="margin-top:24pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman" ALIGN="center"><B>WSFS REPORTS 2Q 2015 EPS OF $0.43; </B></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman" ALIGN="center"><B>CORE NET REVENUE GREW 16% ANNUALIZED; AND </B></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman" ALIGN="center"><B>LOANS GREW 13% ANNUALIZED OVER 1Q 2015 </B></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B>WILMINGTON, Del.</B>, &#151; WSFS Financial Corporation (Nasdaq: WSFS), the parent company of WSFS Bank, reported net income of $12.2 million, or $0.43 per
diluted common share for the second quarter of 2015 compared to net income of $12.7 million, or $0.46 per share for the second quarter of 2014 and net income of $12.9 million, or $0.45 per share for the first quarter of 2015. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Net income for the first six months of 2015 was $25.1 million, or $0.88 per diluted common share, as compared to $29.6 million, or $1.08 per share for the
same period of 2014. Results for 2014 include a one-time tax benefit of $6.7 million, or $0.24 per share. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B>Highlights for the second quarter of 2015:
</B></P> <P STYLE="font-size:6pt;margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt">&nbsp;</P>
<TABLE STYLE="BORDER-COLLAPSE:COLLAPSE; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt" BORDER="0" CELLPADDING="0" CELLSPACING="0" WIDTH="100%">
<TR>
<TD WIDTH="4%">&nbsp;</TD>
<TD WIDTH="3%" VALIGN="top" ALIGN="left">&#149;</TD>
<TD WIDTH="1%" VALIGN="top">&nbsp;</TD>
<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top">Core<SUP STYLE="font-size:85%; vertical-align:top">(n)</SUP> net revenue (excluding securities gains and a special FHLB dividend) increased $2.4 million, or 4% (not annualized), from the first quarter of 2015, and 12%
from the second quarter of 2014, reflecting strong organic growth. </TD></TR></TABLE> <P STYLE="font-size:6pt;margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt">&nbsp;</P>
<TABLE STYLE="BORDER-COLLAPSE:COLLAPSE; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt" BORDER="0" CELLPADDING="0" CELLSPACING="0" WIDTH="100%">
<TR>
<TD WIDTH="4%">&nbsp;</TD>
<TD WIDTH="3%" VALIGN="top" ALIGN="left">&#149;</TD>
<TD WIDTH="1%" VALIGN="top">&nbsp;</TD>
<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top">Net revenue growth included an increase in core<SUP STYLE="font-size:85%; vertical-align:top">(n)</SUP> fee income of $1.3 million, or 6% (not annualized), from the first quarter of 2015, from organic growth and
seasonal increases. </TD></TR></TABLE> <P STYLE="font-size:6pt;margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt">&nbsp;</P>
<TABLE STYLE="BORDER-COLLAPSE:COLLAPSE; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt" BORDER="0" CELLPADDING="0" CELLSPACING="0" WIDTH="100%">
<TR>
<TD WIDTH="4%">&nbsp;</TD>
<TD WIDTH="3%" VALIGN="top" ALIGN="left">&#149;</TD>
<TD WIDTH="1%" VALIGN="top">&nbsp;</TD>
<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top">Expenses declined slightly from the first quarter of 2015, and along with the robust revenue increases mentioned above, this resulted in significantly improved operating leverage, efficiency and pre-tax, pre-provision
net revenue. </TD></TR></TABLE>

<P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B>Notable items: </B></P> <P STYLE="font-size:6pt;margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt">&nbsp;</P>

<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top">WSFS recorded $686,000 (pre-tax) or $0.02 per share (after-tax) in expenses related to corporate development activities during the second quarter of 2015, primarily related to the pending Alliance Bancorp acquisition.

<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top">A $9.1 million substandard loan and troubled debt restructuring (TDR) was placed on nonaccrual status during the second quarter of 2015. This event added $3.6 million in incremental loan loss provision in the second
quarter, or an $0.08 per share negative impact. </TD></TR></TABLE> <P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B>CEO outlook and commentary: </B></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Mark A. Turner, President and CEO, said, &#147;Despite a one-off credit setback, our second quarter results reflect solid fundamental performance. We continue
to see increases in net interest income driven by good growth in our loan portfolio. We have also seen strong growth in our fee income driven by bank-related businesses of Cash Connect, Wealth Management and mortgage banking. Expenses were well
managed and broad loan portfolio credit quality statistics showed improvement. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">&#147;Additionally our continued focus on innovation, growth and serving
our Customers was demonstrated in the quarter as we announced several new digital products and services. These services include WSFS Mobile Cash, our cardless ATM access, WSFS Everyday Pay<SUP STYLE="font-size:85%; vertical-align:top">SM</SUP>, WSFS
Business Mobile Banking and our strategic alliance with ZenBanx to provide mobile, multi-currency deposit accounts, and are responsive to Customers&#146; and market needs. </P>

</TD>
<TD VALIGN="bottom">&nbsp;&nbsp;</TD>
<TD VALIGN="top"> <P STYLE="font-size:12pt;margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt">&nbsp;</P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B></B>WSFS Bank Center</P>

 <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">&#147;We have made steady progress towards, and remain committed to achieving our strategic plan goals,
including a core and sustainable 1.20% ROA by the end of the fourth quarter of 2015.&#148; </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B>Second Quarter 2015 Discussion of Financial Results
</B></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B>Continued solid growth in net interest income </B></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Net interest income for the second quarter of 2015 was $39.1 million, a $273,000, or 1% (not annualized), increase from the first quarter of 2015 while the net
interest margin was 3.71%. The first quarter of 2015 included a special $808,000 FHLB dividend which added 8 basis points (bps) to the margin that quarter. Excluding this special dividend, net interest income increased $1.1 million, or 3% (not
annualized) compared to the first quarter of 2015, primarily due to sizable loan growth; and the net interest margin decreased 3 bps as a result of the continued interest rate environment and competitive pricing pressures. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Compared to the second quarter of 2014, net interest income increased $3.6 million, or 10%, while the net interest margin increased 7 bps. These substantial
year-over-year increases were primarily due to loan growth from both successful acquisition and organic growth. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B>Broad-based loan growth accelerates
</B></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">At June&nbsp;30, 2015, WSFS&#146; net loan portfolio increased $107.5 million, or 3% (not annualized), to $3.34 billion when compared to
March&nbsp;31, 2015. This quarter&#146;s increase came entirely from organic growth and was spread across almost all loan categories, with noteworthy growth in the commercial real estate ($48.8 million) and construction ($48.4 million) portfolios.
</P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Compared to the second quarter of 2014, net loans increased $315.0 million, or 10%, despite a competitive market and the impact of paydowns/payoffs of
problem loans over the past year as the economy has improved. This growth was achieved through organic growth and $176.0 million in loans from the September 2014 First National Bank of Wyoming (FNBW) acquisition. </P>

<TD>&nbsp;</TD></TR>
</TABLE> <P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B>Credit quality remains strong despite one problem loan </B></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Credit quality remained strong during the second quarter of 2015 despite the impact of one $9.1 million Commercial&nbsp;&amp; Industrial (C&amp;I) problem loan
relationship previously classified as substandard and accruing TDR, which was moved to nonaccruing status during the second quarter of 2015. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Total
nonperforming assets were $46.2 million at June&nbsp;30, 2015, a $3.1 million, or 6% (not annualized), improvement from March&nbsp;31, 2015 and delinquencies improved 26% (not annualized), to a low 0.48% of gross loans at June&nbsp;30, 2015 (this
ratio includes nonperforming delinquencies). Classified loans declined and the ratio of total classified loans to Tier 1 capital plus allowance for loan losses (ALLL) also improved to 18.33% from 21.14% at March&nbsp;31, 2015 and 30.60% at
June&nbsp;30, 2014. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Net charge-offs for the second quarter of 2015 were $2.5 million, or 0.29% of total net loans on an annualized basis (including $1.9
million relating to the nonaccruing C&amp;I relationship mentioned above). Total credit costs (provision for loan losses, loan workout expenses, OREO expenses and other credit reserves) were $4.0 million during the quarter ended June&nbsp;30, 2015
(including the $3.6 million for the nonaccruing C&amp;I relationship mentioned above), an increase from $883,000 in the previous quarter and $627,000 in the second quarter of 2014. </P>

<TD VALIGN="top"> <P STYLE="font-size:12pt;margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt">&nbsp;</P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B></B>WSFS Bank Center</P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:1pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">500&nbsp;Delaware&nbsp;Avenue,&nbsp;Wilmington, Delaware 19801</P></TD>

<TD NOWRAP VALIGN="top">&nbsp;&nbsp;</TD></TR></TABLE> <p STYLE="margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt ; font-size:8pt">&nbsp;</P>
 <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">The ALLL grew to $40.8 million at June&nbsp;30, 2015 from $39.5 million in the first quarter of 2015,
reflecting broadly improved portfolio statistics offset by growth in the loan portfolio as well as the expected loss on the additional nonaccruing loan. The ratio of the ALLL to total gross loans remained flat at 1.22% at June&nbsp;30, 2015 compared
to March&nbsp;31, 2015 and is a healthy 147% of nonaccruing loans. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B>Total customer funding reflects continued strength in relationship accounts
</B></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Total customer funding increased $14.4 million from March&nbsp;31, 2015. This was mainly due to a $65.1 million, or 9% (annualized), increase in core
deposits which was partially offset by a decrease of $50.9 million in time deposits. The decrease in time deposits was generally the result of allowing older, higher-rate CDs to run-off as a part of net interest margin management. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Total customer funding increased by $387.0 million, or 13%, from June&nbsp;30, 2014 to $3.36 billion at June&nbsp;30, 2015. The increase was driven by a
$418.4 million, or 17%, increase in core deposits which was partially offset by a $28.4 million decrease in time deposits, as discussed above. Included in the year-over-year growth was $228.8 million in total customer funding from the September 2014
FNBW acquisition. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Core deposits now represent a robust 87% of total customer funding, and no-cost and low-cost relationship checking deposit accounts
represent a strong 47% of total customer funding. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">The following table summarizes customer funding balances and composition at June&nbsp;30, 2015 compared
to prior periods: </P> <P STYLE="font-size:12pt;margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt">&nbsp;</P>

 <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B>Fee income reflects strong growth over prior quarter </B></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Fee income (noninterest income) increased by $1.3 million, or 6% (not annualized), to $22.5 million compared to the first quarter of 2015. The increase
included increases in investment management and fiduciary revenue of $614,000 and credit/debit card and ATM income of $435,000. The overall increase from the prior quarter is attributable to organic growth and typical seasonality in fees. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">When compared to the same period a year ago, fee income (noninterest income) increased $2.8 million, or 14%. This was the result of growth in both banking and
banking-related businesses and included increases in investment management and fiduciary revenue of $1.4 million, mortgage banking activities of $565,000 and credit/debit card and ATM income of $452,000. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Fee income is now a robust 36% of total revenue and is well diversified among various sources: traditional banking, mortgage banking, wealth management and
ATM services (Cash Connect). </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B>Noninterest expense reflects ongoing expense management </B></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Noninterest expense for the second quarter of 2015 was $38.7 million, a decrease of $259,000 from $38.9 million in the first quarter of 2015. The decrease was
primarily due to a $665,000 decrease in salaries, benefits and other compensation from good expense management and the first quarter has typical seasonal increases for higher employer costs such as higher vacation accrual costs, 401(k) matching
costs and certain employer-paid taxes. Marketing expense increased during the second quarter of 2015 to support growth and the introduction of the aforementioned new products and services. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">When compared to the second quarter of 2014, noninterest expense increased $3.4 million. Excluding notable items in both periods,<SUP
STYLE="font-size:85%; vertical-align:top">(n)</SUP> noninterest expense increased $2.9 million, or 8%. The increase was primarily to support robust organic growth and the September 2014 acquisition of FNBW. </P>

 <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B>Selected Business Segments (included in previous results): </B></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B><I>Wealth Management segment fee revenue grew by 30% over the prior year </I></B></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">The Wealth Management segment provides a broad array of fiduciary, investment management, credit and deposit products to clients through four
businesses.&nbsp;<B>WSFS Wealth Investments</B> provides insurance and brokerage products primarily to our retail banking clients.&nbsp;<B>Cypress Capital Management, LLC</B> is a registered investment advisor with approximately $655 million in
assets under management (AUM). Cypress&#146; primary market segment is high net worth individuals, offering a &#145;balanced&#146; investment style focused on preservation of capital and providing for current income. <B>Christiana Trust</B>, with
$8.86 billion in assets under management and administration, provides fiduciary and investment services to personal trust clients, and trustee, agency, bankruptcy, custodial and commercial domicile services to corporate and institutional
clients.&nbsp;<B>WSFS Private Banking</B> serves high net worth clients by delivering credit and deposit products and partnering with other business units to deliver investment management and fiduciary products and services. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Total Wealth Management revenue (net interest income, investment management and fiduciary revenue and other fee income) was $9.0 million during the second
quarter of 2015.&nbsp;This represented an increase of $1.7 million, or 24% compared to the second quarter of 2014 and an increase of $803,000, or 10% (not annualized), compared to the first quarter of 2015.&nbsp;Included in this increase, fee
revenue increased $1.4 million, or 30%, compared to the second quarter of 2014 and $638,000, or 12% (not annualized), compared to the first quarter of 2015. The year-over-year and quarterly growth reflects the continued expansion of several Wealth
business lines, with particular strength in corporate bankruptcy and securitization trustee appointments and retail brokerage services. </P>

 <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Total segment noninterest expense (including intercompany allocations of expense and provision for loan
losses and credit costs) was $5.9 million during the second quarter of 2015 compared to $4.4 million during the second quarter of 2014 and $4.9 million during the first quarter of 2015. The second quarter of 2015 noninterest expenses were impacted
by legal and consulting fees and seasonal client tax return preparation costs totaling $680,000. Excluding these fees in each year, noninterest expense increased $903,000 compared to the second quarter of 2014 and $41,000 from the first quarter of
2015. These year-over-year increases are primarily due to higher legal, consulting and compensation costs necessary to support the robust growth and volume-related commissions and transaction charges. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Pre-tax income for the Wealth Management segment in the second quarter of 2015 was $3.1 million compared to $2.8 million in the second quarter of 2014 and
$3.3 million in the first quarter of 2015. Excluding the legal fees and seasonal tax expenses discussed above in each year, pre-tax income for the second quarter of 2015 was $3.7 million compared to $3.1 million in the second quarter of 2014 and
$3.3 million in the first quarter of 2015. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B><I>Cash Connect results reflect meaningful growth over 2014 </I></B></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">The Cash Connect<SUP STYLE="font-size:85%; vertical-align:top">&reg;</SUP> segment is a premier provider of ATM vault cash and related services in the United
States. Cash Connect<SUP STYLE="font-size:85%; vertical-align:top">&reg;</SUP> services over $557 million in vault cash in over 15,900 non-bank ATMs nationwide and also operates approximately 450 ATMs for WSFS Bank, which has the largest branded ATM
network in Delaware. </P>

 <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Cash Connect<SUP STYLE="font-size:85%; vertical-align:top">&reg;</SUP> recorded $6.9 million in net revenue
(fee income less funding costs) during the second quarter of 2015, an increase of $459,000 from the $6.4 million reported in the first quarter of 2015, reflecting continued organic and seasonal growth. Net revenue also increased $712,000, or 12%,
compared to the second quarter of 2014. Noninterest expenses (including intercompany allocations of expense) were $5.0 million during the second quarter of 2015, an increase of $42,000 compared to the first quarter of 2015 and an increase of
$579,000 from the second quarter of 2014. Cash Connect<SUP STYLE="font-size:85%; vertical-align:top">&reg;</SUP> reported pre-tax income of $1.9 million for the second quarter of 2015, compared to $1.7 million in the second quarter of 2014 and $1.6
million in the first quarter of 2015. The year-over-year results reflect continued growth in the business, offset partially by investments in new products and infrastructure to support growth. Most recently, on June&nbsp;25, 2015, Cash Connect
introduced &#147;WSFS Mobile Cash&#148;, offering security, convenience and speed in digital access to cash. It allows customers to securely withdraw cash from ATMs by using our WSFS Mobile Banking App. WSFS is first in the region and fourth in the
United States to provide this service. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B>Income taxes </B></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">The Company recorded a $6.9 million income tax provision in the second quarter of 2015 compared to a $7.3 million tax provision in the first quarter of 2015
and a $7.1 million tax provision in the second quarter of 2014. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">The effective tax rate was 36.0% in the second quarter of 2015, 36.2% in the first
quarter of 2015 and 35.8% in the second quarter of 2014. The slight increase in the effective tax rates for the first and second quarters of 2015 are principally due to certain nondeductible expenses associated with our pending acquisition of
Alliance Bancorp. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B>Capital management </B></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">WSFS&#146;
total stockholders&#146; equity decreased $5.1 million to $500.4 million at June&nbsp;30, 2015 from $505.5 million at March&nbsp;31, 2015, as a result of Company earnings offset by the Company&#146;s ongoing stock buyback program and a decrease in
the unrealized gains on the Company&#146;s available-for-sale investment portfolio. </P>

<TD VALIGN="top"> <P STYLE="font-size:12pt;margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt">&nbsp;</P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B></B>WSFS Bank Center</P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:1pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">500&nbsp;Delaware&nbsp;Avenue,&nbsp;Wilmington, Delaware 19801</P></TD>

 <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">For the same reasons, WSFS&#146; tangible common
equity<SUP STYLE="font-size:85%; vertical-align:top">(n)</SUP> decreased to $443.3 million at June&nbsp;30, 2015 from $448.1 million at March&nbsp;31, 2015. WSFS&#146; tangible common equity to asset
ratio<SUP STYLE="font-size:85%; vertical-align:top">(n)</SUP> decreased by 34 basis points to 8.83%. Tangible common book value per share<SUP STYLE="font-size:85%; vertical-align:top">(n)</SUP> was $15.88 at June&nbsp;30, 2015, a $0.03 increase from
March&nbsp;31, 2015 due to the impact of the above and share repurchases discussed below. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">At June&nbsp;30, 2015, WSFS Bank&#146;s Tier I leverage ratio
of 10.59%, Common Equity Tier 1 capital ratio of 12.60%, Tier 1 capital ratio of 12.60% and total capital ratio of 13.60%, were all substantially in excess of the &#147;well-capitalized&#148; regulatory benchmarks. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">During the third quarter of 2014, the WSFS Board of Directors approved a stock buyback program of up to 5% of total outstanding shares of common
stock.&nbsp;In the second quarter of 2015, WSFS repurchased 455,402 shares of common stock at an average price of $25.81.&nbsp;WSFS has repurchased the equivalent of 839,582 shares to date under this program at an average equivalent price of $25.75
and has 569,818 shares, or approximately 2% of outstanding shares remaining to repurchase under this current authorization.</P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">During the first quarter of
2015, the WSFS Board of Directors also declared a three-for-one stock split in our common stock in the form of a stock dividend of two shares for each issued and outstanding share of common stock. The stock dividend was paid on May&nbsp;18, 2015 to
stockholders of record as of May&nbsp;4, 2015.</P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Finally, the Board of Directors approved a quarterly cash dividend of $0.05 per share of common
stock.&nbsp;This dividend will be paid on August&nbsp;21, 2015, to shareholders of record as of August&nbsp;7, 2015. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B>Second quarter 2015 earnings
release conference call </B></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Management will conduct a conference call to review second quarter results at 1:00 p.m. Eastern Time (ET) on Friday,
July&nbsp;24, 2015. Interested parties may listen to this call by dialing 1-877-312-5857. A rebroadcast of the conference call will be available two hours after the completion of the call until August&nbsp;8, 2015, by dialing 1-855-859-2056 and
using Conference ID 82950073. </P>

 <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B>About WSFS Financial Corporation </B></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">WSFS Financial Corporation is a multi-billion dollar financial services company. Its primary subsidiary, WSFS Bank, is the oldest, locally-managed bank and
trust company headquartered in Delaware with $5.1 billion in assets on its balance sheet and $9.5 billion in fiduciary assets, including approximately $1.2 billion in assets under management. WSFS operates from 56 offices located in Delaware (45),
Pennsylvania (9), Virginia (1)&nbsp;and Nevada (1)&nbsp;and provides comprehensive financial services including commercial banking, retail banking and trust and wealth management. Other subsidiaries or divisions include <U>Christiana Trust</U>, WSFS
Wealth Investments, <U>Cypress Capital Management, LLC</U>, <U>Cash Connect</U><SUP STYLE="font-size:85%; vertical-align:top">&reg;</SUP>, <U>Array Financial</U> and Arrow Land Transfer. Serving the Delaware Valley since 1832, WSFS Bank is the
seventh oldest bank in the United States continuously operating under the same name. For more information, please visit <U>www.wsfsbank.com</U>. </P>

<TD WIDTH="4%" VALIGN="top" ALIGN="left">(j)</TD>
<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top">Nonperforming loans are included in average balance computations. </TD></TR></TABLE>
<TABLE STYLE="BORDER-COLLAPSE:COLLAPSE; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt" BORDER="0" CELLPADDING="0" CELLSPACING="0" WIDTH="100%">
<TR>
<TD WIDTH="4%" VALIGN="top" ALIGN="left">(k)</TD>
<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top">The difference between projected amounts of interest-sensitive assets and interest-sensitive liabilities repricing within one year divided by total assets, based on a current interest rate scenario. </TD></TR></TABLE>
<TABLE STYLE="BORDER-COLLAPSE:COLLAPSE; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt" BORDER="0" CELLPADDING="0" CELLSPACING="0" WIDTH="100%">
<TR>
<TD WIDTH="4%" VALIGN="top" ALIGN="left">(l)</TD>
<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top">Includes loans held-for-sale. </TD></TR></TABLE>
<TABLE STYLE="BORDER-COLLAPSE:COLLAPSE; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt" BORDER="0" CELLPADDING="0" CELLSPACING="0" WIDTH="100%">
<TR>
<TD WIDTH="4%" VALIGN="top" ALIGN="left">(m)</TD>
<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top">Includes seasonal Associates, when applicable. </TD></TR></TABLE>
<TABLE STYLE="BORDER-COLLAPSE:COLLAPSE; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt" BORDER="0" CELLPADDING="0" CELLSPACING="0" WIDTH="100%">
<TR>
<TD WIDTH="4%" VALIGN="top" ALIGN="left">(n)</TD>
<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top">The Company uses non-GAAP (Generally Accepted Accounting Principles) financial information in its analysis of the Company&#146;s performance. This non-GAAP data should be considered in addition to results prepared in
accordance with GAAP, and is not a substitute for, or superior to, GAAP results. See page 16. </TD></TR></TABLE>
<TABLE STYLE="BORDER-COLLAPSE:COLLAPSE; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt" BORDER="0" CELLPADDING="0" CELLSPACING="0" WIDTH="100%">
<TR>
<TD WIDTH="4%" VALIGN="top" ALIGN="left">(o)</TD>
<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top">Beginning in 2015, the annualization method used to calculate net interest margin was changed to actual/actual from 30/360. All periods net interest margin calculations were updated to reflect this change.
</TD></TR></TABLE>
<TABLE STYLE="BORDER-COLLAPSE:COLLAPSE; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt" BORDER="0" CELLPADDING="0" CELLSPACING="0" WIDTH="100%">
<TR>
<TD WIDTH="4%" VALIGN="top" ALIGN="left">(p)</TD>
<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top">All stock information has been adjusted for the 3 for 1 stock dividend completed on May&nbsp;18, 2015. </TD></TR></TABLE>
